كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها وسدله والتثاؤب وتغميض عينيه وقيام الإمام لا سجوده في الطاق وانفراد الإمام على خرقة وكل ذلك مكروه . كذا في غاية البيان وفي الظهيرية ويكره الاعتجار وهو لف العمامة حول رأسه وإبداء الهامة كما يفعله الشطار اهـ. وفي المحيط ويكره الاعتجار لأنه عليه السلام نهى عنه وهو أن يكور عمامته ويترك وسط رأسه مكشوفاً كهيئة الأشرار . وقيل : أن يتنقب بعمامته فيغطي أنفه كمعجز النساء إما لأجل الحر أو البرد أو للتكبر وهو مكروه لقول ابن عباس : لا يغطي الرجل وهو يصلي .اهـ. وفي المغرب : وتفسير من قال هو أن يلف العمامة على رأسه ويبدي الهامة أقرب لأنه مأخوذ من معجر المرأة وهو ثوب كالعصابة تلفه المرأة على استدارة رأسها اهـ. والمعجر على وزن منبر وعلل كراهة الاعتجار الإمام الولوالجي بأنه تشبه بأهل الكتاب قال : وهو مكروه خارج الصلاة ففيها أولى قوله وكف ثويه للحديث السابق سواء كان من بين يديه أو خلفه عند الانحطاط للسجود والكف هو الضم والجمع ولأن فيه ترك سنة اليد، وذكر في المغرب عن بعضهم أن الائتزار فوق القميص من الكف .اهـ. فعلى هذا يكره أن يصلي مشدود الوسط فوق القميص ونحوه أيضاً وقد صرح به في العتابية معلللاً بأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب لكن في الخلاصة أنه لا يكره . كذا في شرح منية المصلي. ويدخل أيضاً في كف الثوب تشمير كميه كما في فتح القدير وظاهره الإطلاق وفي الخلاصة ومنية المصلي قيد الكراهة بأن يكون رافعاً كميه إلى المرفقين وظاهره أنه لا يكره إذا كان يرفعهما إلى ما دونهما والظاهر الإطلاق لصدق كف الثوب على الكل. وذكر في المجتبى في كراهة تشمير الكمين قولين، وذكر في القنية أن القول بإمساك الكمين أحوط ولا يخفي ما فيه . وفي مذهب مالك تفصيل قد كنت رأيته لأئمتنا في بعض الفتاوى ولم يحضرني تعيينها الآن وهو أنه يكره إن كان للصلاة لا إذا كان لأجل شغل ثم حضرته الصلاة فصلى وهو على تلك الهيئة ومن كف الثوب رفعه كيلا يتترب كما في منية المصلي، وقيل لا بأس بصونه عن التراب كما في المجتبى . من قوله (وسدله) لنهيه عليه السلام عنه كما أخرجه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه. . يقال سدل الثوب سدلاً من باب طلب إذا أرسله من غير أن يضم جانبه . وقيل : هو أن يلقيه على رأسه ويرخيه على منكبيه وأسدل خطأ . كذا في المغرب. وذكر في البدائع أن الكرخي فسره بأن يجعل ثوبه على رأسه أو على كتفيه ويرسل أطرافه من جوانبه إذا لم يكن عليه سراويل. تشمیر قوله : (والظاهر الإطلاق فيه نظر إن يكن سنده ما ذكره عن فتح القدير لأن الكمال وإن أطلق هنا قد قيد كلامه فيما بعد عند استطراد فروع ذكرها فقال : وتكره الصلاة أيضاً مع الكم عن الساعد فلا مخالفة بينه وبين الخلاصة والمنية . كذا في الشرنبلالية تأمل قوله : (وفي مذهب مالك تفصيل الخ) قال في النهر المذكور في القنية أنه لو شمر كميه لعمل كان يعمله قبل الصلاة اختلفوا في الكراهة وهو ظاهر في الكراهة فيما لو شمر لها .اهـ وعبارة القنية : واختلف فيمن صلى وقد شمر كميه لعمل كان يعمله قبل الصلاة أو هيئته ذلك. وفيها أيضاً عن نجم الأئمة: وكان وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يكره السدل على القميص وعلى الإزار وقال : لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب . فإن كان السدل بدون السراويل فكراهته لاحتمال كشف العورة عند الركوع ، وإن كان مع الأزار فكراهته لأجل التشبه بأهل الكتاب فهو مكروه مطلقاً، سواء كان للخيلاء أو لغيره للنهي من غير فصل اهـ. وفي فتح القدير أن السدل يصدق على أن يكون المنديل مرسلاً من كتفيه كما يعتاده كثير فينبغي لمن على عنقه منديل أن يضعه عند الصلاة، ويصدق أيضاً على لبس القباء من غير إدخال اليدين في كميه وقد صرح بالكراهة فيه .اهـ. وكذا صرح في النهاية بإدخال القباء المذكور في السدل وعزاه إلى مبسوط شيخ الإسلام والخلاصة لكن الذي في خلاصة الفتاوى : المصلي إذا كان لابساً شقة أو فرجيه ولم يدخل يديه اختلف المتأخرون في الكراهة والمختار أنه لا يكره اهـ. وظاهر ما في فتح القدير أن الشد الذي يعتاد وضعه على الكتفين إذا أرسل طرفاً على صدره وطرفاً على ظهره لا يخرج عن الكراهية فإنه عين الوضع، وظاهر كلامهم يقتضي أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون الثوب محفوظاً من الوقوع أو لا، فعلى هذا يكره في الطيلسان الذي يجعل على الرأس، وقد صرح به في شرح الوقاية وصرح العامة الحلبي بأن محل كراهة السدل عند عدم العذر، وأما عند العذر فلا كراهة وأنه إن كان للتكبر فهو مكروه مطلقاً . واختلف المشايخ في كراهة السدل خارج الصلاة كما في الدراية وصحح في القنية من باب الكراهية أنه لا يكره. ومن المكروه اشتمال الصماء لما رواه أبو داود عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله ( إذا كان لأحدكم ثوبان فليصل فيهما فإن لم يكن إلا ثوب فليتزر به ولا يشتمل اشتمال اليهود ) اهـ . واشتمال اليهود هو الصماء وهو إدارة الثوب على الجسد من غير إخراج اليد سمي بها لعدم منفذ يخرج يده منها كالصخرة الصماء، وفسرها في المحيط بأن يجمع طرفي ثوبه ويخرجهما تحت إحدى يديه على أحد كتفيه اهـ. وقيده في البدائع بأن لا يكون عليه سراويل . وإنما كره لأنه لا يؤمن انكشاف العورة، ومحمد رحمه الله فصل بين الاضطباغ ولبسة الصماء فقال : إنما تكره الصماء إذا لم يكن عليه إزار فإن كان عليه إزار فهو اضطباع لأن يدخل طرفي ثوبه تحت إحدى ضبعيه وهو مكروه لأنه لبس أهل الكبر اهـ. يرسل كميه في الصلاة ويقول لأن في إمساكهما كف الثوب وأنه مكروه ثم رمز إلى مجد الأئمة وغيره أنهم كانوا يمسكون ذلك. قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : وهو الأحوط .اهـ. قوله : (والمختار أنه لا يكره) قال الرملي : ومثله في البزازيه واختار قاضيخان وغيره أنه يكره وهو الصحيح. كذا ذكره الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي قوله: (وصحح في القنية أنه لا يكره قال في النهر أي تحريماً وإلا فمقتضى ما أنه يكره تنزيهاً .اهـ. وما مر هو قوله لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب. قال الشيخ إسماعيل : وفيه بحث لأن الظاهر من كلامهم أن تخصيص أهل الكتاب بفعله معتبر فيه كونه في الصلاة فلا يظهر التشبه وكراهته خارجها فليتأمل.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on What Invalidates Prayer and What is Disliked in It. And the Sadl (letting garment hang loosely), yawning, closing eyes, the imam standing (but not prostrating) in the arch, the imam being alone on a piece of cloth – all that is disliked (makruh). Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan and in al-Zahiriyya. And Ihtijar is disliked, which is wrapping the turban around the head and exposing the crown, as the ruffians do. In al-Muhit: Ihtijar is disliked because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade it, and it is to roll up the turban and leave the middle of the head uncovered like the wicked. And it is said: it is to cover the nose with the turban like women's veils, either due to heat or cold or arrogance, and it is disliked due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'A man should not cover (his face) while praying.' In al-Mughrib: the interpretation of those who say it is wrapping the turban on the head and exposing the crown is more likely because it is derived from mi'jar of women, which is a cloth like a headband that a woman wraps around her head. Al-Mi'jar is on the pattern of minbar. Imam al-Walwaliji reasoned the dislike of Ihtijar as resembling the People of the Book. He said: it is disliked outside prayer, so inside it is more so. His statement: 'and folding his garment (kaff thawbayh)' due to the previous hadith, whether from in front of him or behind him when lowering for prostration. Kaff is to fold and gather. And because it abandons the sunna of the hands. It is mentioned in al-Mughrib from some that wearing the izaar over the qamis is from kaff. Thus, it is disliked to pray with the waist tied over the qamis and the like. It is explicitly stated in al-Atabiyya, reasoned as the practice of the People of the Book, but in al-Khulasa it is not disliked. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Also included in kaff al-thawb is rolling up the sleeves, as in Fath al-Qadir, and its apparent meaning is general. In al-Khulasa and Munyat al-Musalli, the dislike is restricted to raising the sleeves to the elbows; apparently it is not disliked if raised less than that, but the general position is that it applies to all, because 'kaff al-thawb' applies to all. In al-Mujtaba there are two opinions on the dislike of rolling up the sleeves. In al-Quniyya, it is stated that holding the sleeves is more cautious (ahwat). In the Maliki school there is a detail: it is disliked if done for the prayer; if done for work and then one prays in that state, it is not disliked. And from kaff al-thawb is lifting it to avoid dust, as in Munyat al-Musalli, and it is said there is no harm in protecting it from dust, as in al-Mujtaba. From his statement: (and Sadl) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade it, as recorded by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim and he declared it authentic. It is said: sadl al-thawb is to let it hang without folding its side. And it is said: it is to throw it over the head and let it down over the shoulders, and 'asdala' is a mistake. Thus in al-Mughrib. It is mentioned in al-Bada'i that al-Karkhi interpreted it as placing the garment on the head or shoulders and letting its ends hang from the sides if there is no sirwal. Tashmir: His statement: (and the general position is debatable) if its authority is what he mentioned from Fath al-Qadir, because al-Kamal ibn al-Humam, although he gave a general statement here, later restricted his words when discussing branches, saying: 'Prayer with the sleeve above the forearm is also disliked.' So there is no contradiction between him and al-Khulasa and Munyat al-Musalli. Thus in al-Sharnabaliyya. His statement: (and in the Maliki school there is a detail etc.) He said in al-Nahr: mentioned in al-Quniyya that if one rolled up his sleeves for work he was doing before prayer, there is disagreement on the dislike – and it is apparent that it is disliked if done for the prayer itself. The expression of al-Quniyya: 'And they differed about one who prays while having rolled up his sleeves for work he was doing before prayer, or that was his habit.' And in it also from Najm al-A'imma: And from Abu Hanifa that he disliked sadl over the qamis and over the izaar, and he said: because it is the practice of the People of the Book. If the sadl is without a sirwal, then its dislike is due to the possibility of the 'awra being exposed during ruku'; if with an izaar, then its dislike is due to resembling the People of the Book. So it is disliked absolutely, whether out of arrogance or otherwise, due to the prohibition without distinction. In Fath al-Qadir: Sadl applies to a handkerchief hanging from the shoulders as many do, so one who has a handkerchief around his neck should remove it when praying. It also applies to wearing a cloak (qaba') without inserting the hands into its sleeves, and he explicitly stated its dislike. Similarly, in al-Nihaya, the mentioned cloak is included in sadl, and he attributed it to the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam and al-Khulasa. But in Khulasat al-Fatawa: 'The one praying, if he is wearing a shiqqa or farjiyya and did not insert his hands, the later scholars differed on the dislike, and the chosen view is that it is not disliked.' The apparent meaning of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the shadd (a scarf) habitually placed on the shoulders, if one end is let down on the chest and the other on the back, does not escape dislike, for it is exactly that position. The apparent meaning of their words is that there is no difference whether the garment is prevented from falling or not. Thus, it is disliked in the taylasan placed on the head, as explicitly stated in Sharh al-Wiqaya. And al-Halabi explicitly stated that the place of dislike of sadl is when there is no excuse, and if there is an excuse, there is no dislike, and if it is for arrogance, it is disliked absolutely. The mashayikh differed on the dislike of sadl outside prayer, as in al-Diraya, and in al-Quniyya it is declared authentic that it is not disliked. Among the disliked actions is Ishtimal al-Samma'. For Abu Dawud narrated from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If one of you has two garments, let him pray in them; if he has only one garment, let him wrap it around his waist (yattazir) and not wrap it in the manner of the Jews (ishtimal al-yahud).' And the wrapping of the Jews is al-Samma'. It is the wrapping of the garment around the body without taking out the hands. It is called samma' because there is no outlet for the hands, like a solid rock (sakhra samma'). In al-Muhit, it is interpreted as gathering the two ends of the garment and bringing them under one of his arms onto one shoulder. In al-Bada'i, it is restricted to when there is no sirwal. It is disliked because exposure of the 'awra is not safe from it. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) distinguished between idtiba' and the dress of samma'. He said: 'Samma' is only disliked if there is no izaar; if there is an izaar, then it is idtiba' (wrapping with one shoulder bare) – and that is disliked because it is the dress of the arrogant.' He lets his sleeves hang in prayer and says: because holding them is kaff al-thawb and it is disliked. Then he gestured to Majd al-A'imma and others that they used to hold them. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'That is more cautious (ahwat).' His statement: (and the chosen view is that it is not disliked) al-Ramli said: 'And similar is in al-Bazzaziyya, and Qadi Khan and others chose that it is disliked, and it is the correct view.' Thus mentioned by al-Halabi in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. His statement: (and in al-Quniyya it is declared authentic that it is not disliked) He said in al-Nahr: 'i.e., as tahrimi? Otherwise, the apparent meaning is that it is makruh tanzihi.' And what passed is his statement: 'because it is the practice of the People of the Book.' Shaykh Ismail said: 'There is discussion in this, for the apparent meaning of their words is that the specification of the People of the Book by this action is considered when it is in prayer; so resemblance and its dislike outside prayer are not apparent. So let it be considered.'
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering the chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked (makruh) in it. The author, Ibn Nujaym, expands on several disliked actions, providing definitions, proofs from hadith, and the reasoning (ta'lil) for their rulings. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from primary sources and later scholarly consensus.

First, the text lists general disliked actions: sadl (letting the garment hang loosely), yawning, closing the eyes, the imam standing in an arch without prostrating, and the imam praying alone on a piece of cloth. All are ruled makruh based on prior authoritative works like Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Zahiriyya.

Then focuses on al-Ihtijar (اعتجار): wrapping the turban around the head while leaving the crown exposed, as done by ruffians. The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade it. It is disliked because it resembles wicked people or, according to some interpretations, involves covering the nose like women's veils. Imam al-Walwaliji adds that it is a resemblance to the People of the Book, so it is disliked even outside prayer, and more so inside it.

Next, al-Kaff (كف الثوب): folding or gathering the garment, such as folding the garment in front or behind during prostration. This abandons the sunna of letting the hands hang. Wearing the izaar (waist wrapper) above the qamis (shirt) is considered kaff. Some Hanafi sources differ: 'al-Atabiyya' rules it makruh as resembling the People of the Book, while 'al-Khulasa' says it is not disliked. Ibn Nujaym notes a restriction: raising sleeves to the elbows is makruh, but less than that may be permissible. There are two opinions in 'al-Mujtaba'. The cautious view (ahwat) is to hold the sleeves. The passage also discusses sadl in detail: its definitions, the narration from Abu Dawud and al-Hakim (authenticated), and the opinion of Abu Hanifa that it is makruh over both the qamis and izaar because it is the practice of the People of the Book. If no sirwal (trousers) is worn, the added risk of 'awra exposure during ruku' increases the dislike. Sadl applies to letting a handkerchief or cloak hang loosely. On the issue of sadl outside prayer, there is disagreement; the authenticated view in 'al-Quniyya' is that it is not disliked, but it is still makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful) as some interpret.

Finally, Ishtimal al-Samma' (اشتمال الصماء): wrapping the entire body in a garment without any opening for the hands, similar to the Jewish practice. The hadith from Ibn Umar prohibits it. It is called samma' because it resembles a solid rock (sakhra samma') with no outlet. It is makruh because it may expose the 'awra. Imam Muhammad distinguishes: if there is an izaar underneath, it becomes idtiba' (wrapping with one shoulder bare), which is also disliked as the dress of the arrogant. The passage ends by noting that holding the sleeves during prayer is considered kaff and is disliked, but many early scholars actually held them, so the author says that holding them is more cautious (ahwat).

Key Terms
كف الثوب (kaff al-thawb): Folding or gathering the garment. Includes rolling up sleeves, wearing the izaar over the qamis, and lifting the garment to avoid dust.
اشتمال الصماء (ishtimal al-samma'): Wrapping the entire body in a garment without any opening for the hands, resembling a solid rock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ishtimal al-samma' (wrapping the body in a garment with no hand openings) during prayer if the person is wearing an izaar underneath?
A) It is permissible because the 'awra is covered.
B) It is disliked because it becomes idtiba', the dress of the arrogant.
C) It is recommended because it is modest.
D) It is forbidden because it explicitly violates a Quranic command.

Key Takeaway
Kaff al-thawb and ishtimal al-samma' are makruh in prayer due to abandoning the sunna and resembling non-Muslims; the latter has a distinction between samma' (without izaar) and idtiba' (with izaar), both disliked.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Sadl (Hanging Garment) in Prayer
Ruling on dislike of sadl with explanations based on imitation of Ahl al-Kitab and exposure of 'awrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sadl in prayer and explain the reasons for its dislike, including the role of imitation of Ahl al-Kitab and exposure of 'awrah, as well as the intra-Hanafi differences regarding its scope.

Core Idea
Sadl in prayer is disliked because it resembles Ahl al-Kitab and risks exposing the 'awrah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on letting a garment hang loosely (sadl) during prayer. The source passage, taken from a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, cites Abu Hanifa's explicit dislike and provides reasoning based on both resemblance to non-Muslims and the possibility of uncovering the 'awrah. We will explore the proof, the conditions that affect the ruling, and the differences among later Hanafi scholars on its application inside and outside prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what 'sadl' means in this context and state the hukm (ruling) as per Abu Hanifa. Note that it is makruh (disliked) whether on a shirt or waist-wrapper.
The passage specifies dislike is 'makrahan' from Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited for the dislike. The text states 'because it is the practice of the People of the Book' (صنيع أهل الكتاب). Identify this as a general prohibition of imitation.
The dalil is not a specific hadith but a principle of avoiding tashabbuh bil-kuffar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the practice of Ahl al-Kitab leads to the ruling of dislike. The connection is that sadl is a distinctive practice of non-Muslims, and imitating them in acts of worship is prohibited.
The passage also adds a secondary reason: risk of 'awrah exposure when without trousers.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding sadl outside prayer. Some later scholars hold it is not disliked outside prayer, while others maintain dislike absolutely. The passage notes the chosen view in al-Qunya that it is not disliked outside.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is that it is disliked inside prayer absolutely, and outside only if for pride.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
Determine which position is operative for fatwa. The text indicates that despite some differences, the preferred view is that sadl is disliked in prayer without exception, based on the general nature of the prohibition.
This is supported by citing al-Hidayah and al-Halabi.

وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يكره السدل على القميص وعلى الإزار وقال : لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب . فإن كان السدل بدون السراويل فكراهته لاحتمال كشف العورة عند الركوع ، وإن كان مع الأزار فكراهته لأجل التشبه بأهل الكتاب فهو مكروه مطلقاً، سواء كان للخيلاء أو لغيره للنهي من غير فصل اهـ. وفي فتح القدير أن السدل يصدق على أن يكون المنديل مرسلاً من كتفيه كما يعتاده كثير فينبغي لمن على عنقه منديل أن يضعه عند الصلاة، ويصدق أيضاً على لبس القباء من غير إدخال اليدين في كميه وقد صرح بالكراهة فيه .اهـ. وكذا صرح في النهاية بإدخال القباء المذكور في السدل وعزاه إلى مبسوط شيخ الإسلام والخلاصة لكن الذي في خلاصة الفتاوى : المصلي إذا كان لابساً شقة أو فرجيه ولم يدخل يديه اختلف المتأخرون في الكراهة والمختار أنه لا يكره اهـ. وظاهر ما في فتح القدير أن الشد الذي يعتاد وضعه على الكتفين إذا أرسل طرفاً على صدره وطرفاً على ظهره لا يخرج عن الكراهية فإنه عين الوضع، وظاهر كلامهم يقتضي أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون الثوب محفوظاً من الوقوع أو لا، فعلى هذا يكره في الطيلسان الذي يجعل على الرأس، وقد صرح به في شرح الوقاية وصرح العامة الحلبي بأن محل كراهة السدل عند عدم العذر، وأما عند العذر فلا كراهة وأنه إن كان للتكبر فهو مكروه مطلقاً . واختلف المشايخ في كراهة السدل خارج الصلاة كما في الدراية وصحح في القنية من باب الكراهية أنه لا يكره. ومن المكروه اشتمال الصماء لما رواه أبو داود عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله ( إذا كان لأحدكم ثوبان فليصل فيهما فإن لم يكن إلا ثوب فليتزر به ولا يشتمل اشتمال اليهود ) اهـ . واشتمال اليهود هو الصماء وهو إدارة الثوب على الجسد من غير إخراج اليد سمي بها لعدم منفذ يخرج يده منها كالصخرة الصماء، وفسرها في المحيط بأن يجمع طرفي ثوبه ويخرجهما تحت إحدى يديه على أحد كتفيه اهـ. وقيده في البدائع بأن لا يكون عليه سراويل . وإنما كره لأنه لا يؤمن انكشاف العورة، ومحمد رحمه الله فصل بين الاضطباغ ولبسة الصماء فقال : إنما تكره الصماء إذا لم يكن عليه إزار فإن كان عليه إزار فهو اضطباع لأن يدخل طرفي ثوبه تحت إحدى ضبعيه وهو مكروه لأنه لبس أهل الكبر اهـ.
And from Abu Hanifa that sadi (letting the garment hang) is disliked over the shirt and over the waist-wrapper, and he said: Because it is the practice of the People of the Book. For if the sadi is without trousers, its dislike is due to the possibility of uncovering the ‘awrah during bowing; and if it is with the waist-wrapper, its dislike is for the sake of resembling the People of the Book, so it is absolutely disliked, whether out of pride or otherwise, due to the prohibition without differentiation. End quote. And in Fath al-Qadir, that sadi applies to having a handkerchief hanging from one's shoulders as many are accustomed; so one who has a scarf on his neck should place it during prayer. It also applies to wearing a cloak without inserting the hands into its sleeves, and he explicitly deemed it disliked. End quote. Similarly, in al-Nihaya, the mentioned cloak is included in sadi, attributed to Mabswt of Shaykh al-Islam and al-Khulasah. However, in Khulasat al-Fatawa: The praying person, if wearing a shiqa or farajiyya and did not insert his hands, the later scholars differed regarding the dislike, and the chosen view is that it is not disliked. End quote. And the apparent meaning of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that the scarf customarily placed on the shoulders, if he sends one end to his chest and one end to his back, does not exit from dislike, because it is exactly the same position. The apparent meaning of their words requires that there is no difference between whether the garment is secured from falling or not; thus, it is disliked in the taylasan placed on the head, as explicitly mentioned in Sharh al-Wiqaya. And the general scholar al-Halabi explicitly stated that the locus of dislike of sadi is in the absence of an excuse; as for with an excuse, there is no dislike, and if it is out of arrogance, it is absolutely disliked. And the mashayikh differed regarding the dislike of sadi outside prayer, as in al-Duraya, and it was corrected in al-Qunyatiya that it is not disliked.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on sadi (letting a garment hang loosely) in prayer according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by citing Abu Hanifa's dislike of sadi over a shirt or waist-wrapper, with the reasoning that it resembles the practice of the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab). The dislike is absolute, whether it is done for pride or any other reason, because the prohibition is general. The commentary then distinguishes between cases: if sadi is done without trousers (sirwal), the dislike is heightened due to the risk of exposing the ‘awrah during ruku‘; if done with a waist-wrapper, the dislike is purely due to resemblance to Ahl al-Kitab. Fath al-Qadir further explains that sadi includes having a handkerchief or scarf hanging from the shoulders or wearing a cloak without inserting the hands. Some later scholars (mutā’akhkhirūn) opined that it is not disliked, but the relied-upon view according to some is dislike. The text also discusses the difference between inside and outside prayer, with the correct view (tashih) that outside prayer it is not disliked. However, the preferred position (mu’tamad) in the school is that sadi is disliked even outside prayer, as mentioned by some. The passage also mentions sadi in the context of a taylasan (hood) and the ruling when there is an excuse, where dislike is lifted.

Key Terms
السدل (al-sadl): Letting a garment hang loosely without securing it, such as wearing a cloak without inserting hands or having a scarf hanging from the shoulders.
صنيع أهل الكتاب (ṣanīʿ ahl al-kitāb): Practice or action of the People of the Book (Jews and Christians); emulating them is prohibited in acts of worship.
اشتمال الصماء (ishtimal al-samma'): Wrapping a garment around the body without any opening for the hands, resembling a solid rock; a specific disliked form of dress in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is sadl disliked when done without trousers?
A) Because it resembles Ahl al-Kitab
B) Because it may uncover the 'awrah during ruku'
C) Because it is a sign of laziness
D) Because it invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
Sadl in prayer is disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it imitates non-Muslims and can expose the 'awrah; the dislike is absolute inside prayer, but outside prayer only if for pride.

Ruling on Praying in One or Multiple Garments
Ruling with proof on prayer attire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying in one garment and explain the recommended number of garments with the supporting proof.

Core Idea
Praying in one garment covering the whole body is valid without dislike; three garments are recommended.

Prayer attire is a matter of adab and validity. The Hanafi school addresses common questions: Is it permissible to pray in a single garment? Is there a disliked mode? This passage, citing a hadith from the Sahihayn, establishes that a single garment covering the entire body is perfectly valid and not disliked, while specifying that the recommended practice is to wear three garments. The passage also clarifies situations that are disliked, such as wearing only an izār.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying in one garment that covers the entire body (mutawashshihan). The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) without dislike.
The phrase 'لا بأس' indicates permissibility.
2
Distinguish permissibility from recommendation
The text states it is mustahab (recommended) to pray in three garments: a shirt, an izār, and a turban. This shows a higher virtue while affirming the basic validity of one garment.
Three garments is the sunnah method.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Umar ibn Abi Salama in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim, where the Prophet (PBUH) prayed in one garment in Umm Salama's house.
The hadith is muttafaq 'alayh (agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim).
4
Analyze the dalil
The Prophet's action (fi‘l) indicates permissibility (jawāz). Since the hadith is authentic, it serves as a binding proof. The Hanafi principle holds that the Prophet's voluntary acts are evidence for permissibility unless there is proof of obligation or prohibition.
Dalālah is zanni because it is a fi‘l, not an amr (command).
5
Identify disliked modes
The text mentions that praying in a single izār (waist-wrapper) is permissible but disliked (makruh), and similarly for trousers only or bareheaded out of laziness. These are not covered by the hadith of the single garment because they leave part of the body exposed.
Dislike is tanzihi (not sinful but better to avoid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة وغيرها : لا بأس أن يصلي الرجل في ثوب واحد متوشحاً به جميع بدنه ويؤم كذلك، والمستحب أن يصلي الرجل في ثلاثة أثواب : قميص وإزار وعمامة. أما لو صلى في ثوب واحد متوشحاً به جميع بدنه كإزار الميت تجوز صلاته من غير كراهة. وتفسيره ما يجعله القصار في المقصرة. وإن صلى في إزار واحد يجوز ويكره وكذا في السراويل فقط لغير عذر، وكذا مكشوف الرأس للتهاون والتكاسل لا للخشوع وفسر في الذخيرة التوشيح أن يكون الثوب طويلاً يتوشح به فيجعل بعضه على رأسه وبعضه على منكبيه وعلى كل موضع من بدنه، وذكر في شرح منية المصلي أن ستر المنكبين في الصلاة مستحب يكره تركه تنزيهاً عند أصحابنا، وفسره في المغرب بأن يدخله تحت يده اليمنى ويلقيه على منكبه الأيسر كما يفعله المحرم اهـ. وفسره ابن السكيت بأن يأخذ طرف الثوب الذي ألقاه على منكبه الأيمن من تحت يده اليسرى ويأخذ طرفه الذي ألقاه على الأيسر من تحت يده اليمنى ثم يعقدهما على صدره، وقد ثبت في الصحيحين عن عمر بن أبي سلمة أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي في ثوب واحد في بيت أم سلمة قد ألقى طرفيه على عاتقه، وفي لفظ مشتملاً به واضعاً طرفيه على عاتقيه، وفي لفظ مخالفاً بين طرفيه وفي حديث جابر متوشحاً به، والألفاظ كلها بمعنى واحد كما ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم.
And in al-Khulasa and others: There is no objection to a man praying in one garment, wrapping it around his entire body, and leading the prayer likewise. It is recommended that a man pray in three garments: a shirt, a waist-wrapper, and a turban. But if he prays in one garment wrapping it around his entire body like the shroud of a deceased, his prayer is valid without dislike. Its interpretation is what the launderer places on the press. If he prays in a single waist-wrapper, it is permissible but disliked, and likewise in trousers only without an excuse, and likewise bareheaded out of negligence and laziness, not for humility. And in al-Dhakhira, tawashshuh is defined as the garment being long, he wraps himself with it, placing part on his head and part on his shoulders and on every part of his body. And it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that covering the shoulders in prayer is recommended, leaving it is disliked (tanzihan) according to our school. And in al-Mughrib it is defined as inserting it under his right arm and throwing it over his left shoulder as the muhrim does. And Ibn al-Sikkit defines it as taking the end of the garment he threw over his right shoulder from under his left hand, and taking the end he threw over his left shoulder from under his right hand, then tying them together on his chest. It is confirmed in the Sahihayn from Umar ibn Abi Salama that he saw the Prophet (PBUH) praying in one garment in the house of Umm Salama, having thrown its ends over his shoulders. In another wording: 'wrapping himself with it, placing its ends on his shoulders.' In another wording: 'crossing the ends.' And in the hadith of Jabir: 'wrapping himself with it.' All the wordings have the same meaning, as al-Nawawi mentioned in Sharh Muslim.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
Passage type: ruling with proof. This passage discusses the ruling on clothing during prayer. It begins by stating that praying in one garment covering the entire body (tawashshuh) is permissible without dislike, and it is recommended to pray in three garments: shirt, waist-wrapper, and turban. The text then clarifies that if one prays in a single garment like a shroud, it is valid without dislike. The definition of tawashshuh is given: a long garment wrapped around the body, covering head, shoulders, etc. Covering the shoulders is recommended; leaving them uncovered is disliked (tanzih). The passage provides several definitions of tawashshuh and cites a hadith from the Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) showing the Prophet (PBUH) prayed in one garment, confirming the validity. The hadith is the proof (dalil) that praying in one garment is permissible and not disliked.

Key Terms
متوشحاً (mutawashshihan): Wrapping a garment around the body covering the entire body, a specific mode of dress in prayer
توشيح (tawshīḥ): The act of wrapping a garment around the body in the manner of tawashshuh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying in a single garment that covers the entire body (mutawashshihan)?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Valid without dislike
D) Valid but disliked

Key Takeaway
Praying in one garment covering the whole body is permissible without dislike, and covering the shoulders is recommended.

Disliked Acts: Talaththum and Covering Feet in Prayer
Definition and ruling on disliked acts in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on talaththum and covering feet in prayer, and distinguish between intentional and unintentional covering.

Core Idea
Covering mouth and nose in prayer is disliked; covering feet in sujud is disliked only if intentional.

In this lesson we examine two specific disliked acts (makruhat) in salah: talaththum—covering the mouth and nose—and covering the feet during prostration. The Hanafi position is based on resemblance to Zoroastrian worship and avoidance of unnecessary movement. Understanding the role of intentionality is key to applying these rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Define talaththum
Identify the Arabic term and its precise definition: covering both mouth and nose, not just mouth.
Some incorrectly restrict it to mouth only.
2
Identify the ruling and its basis
State that talaththum is makruh tanzihi (disliked). The reason given is resemblance to Zoroastrians (Majus) during fire worship.
The analogy (tashabbuh) is the effective cause.
3
Analyze the ruling on covering feet in sujud
In al-Khulasa, covering feet intentionally in prostration is disliked. Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi clarifies that unintentional covering is not disliked.
Intentionality is the key shart (condition) for the ruling.
4
Distinguish intentional vs unintentional
If covering occurs without intent (e.g., garment falls), there is no karaha. Deliberately uncovering after covering is also disliked as futile action.
This is an intra-Hanafi nuance from later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المكروه التلثم وتغطية الأنف والوجه في الصلاة لأنه يشبه فعل المجوس حال عبادتهم النيران كذا ذكره الشارح لكن التلثم هو تغطية الأنف والوجه كما في المحيط. وفي الخلاصة : ولو ستر قدميه في السجدة يكره . قوله (وفسره في (المغرب) أي فسر التوشح قوله : (لكن) التلثم الخ) استدراك على الشارح . وحاصله أن التلثم يغني عن قوله وتغطية الأنف والوجه قوله : (ولو ستر قدميه في السجدة يكره) قال الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرح المنية : ولعل مرادهم قصد ذلك لأنه فعل زائد لا فائدة فيه أما لو وقع بغير قصد فلا وجه لكراهته بل يكره تكلف الكشف لأنه اشتغال بما لا فائدة فيه
And from the disliked [acts] is al-talaththum and covering the nose and face in prayer because it resembles the act of the Zoroastrians during their worship of fire, as mentioned by the commentator. But al-talaththum is covering the nose and face as in al-Muhit. And in al-Khulasa: If he covers his feet in prostration, it is disliked. His saying (and he interpreted it in al-Mughrib): i.e., he interpreted tawashshuh. His saying (but al-talaththum etc.) is a correction of the commentator. The summary is that talaththum suffices for his saying and covering the nose and face. His saying: (And if he covers his feet in prostration, it is disliked). Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi said in Sharh al-Munya: Perhaps they intend that [covering] intentionally because it is an extra action with no benefit. But if it happens unintentionally, there is no basis for dislike; rather, making an effort to uncover is disliked because it is an occupation with no benefit.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
Passage type: definition and ruling on disliked acts. This section addresses three disliked acts in prayer: (1) talaththum – covering the mouth and nose, (2) covering the feet during prostration. Talaththum is defined as covering the nose and mouth, and it is disliked because it resembles the practice of Zoroastrians (Majus) who cover their mouths while worshipping fire. The commentary clarifies that covering the feet intentionally is disliked as it is an extra action without benefit; but if it happens unintentionally, there is no dislike. However, deliberately uncovering the feet after they were covered is also disliked due to unnecessary movement. The note on tawashshuh is a correction of the commentator's terminology.

Key Terms
التلثم (al-talaththum): Covering the mouth and nose, disliked in prayer because it resembles Zoroastrians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is talaththum (covering mouth and nose) disliked in prayer?
A) It invalidates prayer
B) It resembles the worship of fire by Zoroastrians
C) It is considered arrogance
D) It prevents proper recitation

Key Takeaway
Talaththum is makruh tanzihi due to resemblance to fire worship; covering feet in sujud is makruh only if intentional.

Yawning in Prayer: Ruling and Etiquette
Ruling on yawning in prayer with proof and etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on yawning in prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the recommended etiquette for suppressing it based on the hadith and its wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
Yawning in prayer is makruh; suppress it by closing the mouth or covering with the back of the hand.

Yawning during prayer is not a nullifier, but it is disliked because it stems from satanic influence. The Prophet (PBUH) instructed us to suppress it as much as possible. This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence from hadith, and the proper manner of covering the mouth if suppression is not possible. We also explore the disagreement about which hand to use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Yawning in prayer is classified as makruh tanzih (disliked but not prohibited). The text states it is disliked even outside prayer according to al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Makruh tanzih means avoidance is rewarded but doing it is not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'التثاؤب من الشيطان فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع' (Yawning is from Satan; when one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible).
The hadith is sahih with qati' thubut but zanni dalala regarding the degree of obligation.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليكظم' indicates wujub or istihbab of suppression, and the attribution to Satan makes the act itself disliked. The command implies that yawning should be avoided if possible.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but here it is interpreted as recommendation due to the nature of the act.
4
Examine the subsidiary ruling
If one cannot suppress the yawn, the proper etiquette is to cover the mouth with the back of the hand or with the sleeve. The hand should be placed with its back outward. If one could bite the lips but instead covers the mouth, it becomes more disliked.
The ruling on covering the mouth is based on a hadith in Abu Dawud prohibiting covering the mouth in prayer without necessity.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on hand preference
There is a minor intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether to use the right or left hand. Al-Halabi noted no clear ruling, but al-Mujtaba specifies right hand when standing, left otherwise.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the core ruling; one may choose based on context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (المصنف والتثاؤب) بالهمز كما في الصحاح. وفي الدر المختار يكره ولو خارجها ذكره مسكين لأنه من الشيطان والأنبياء عليهم السلام محفوظون منه . قوله (والتثاؤب) وهو التنفس الذي ينفتح منه الفم لدفع البخارات وهو ينشأ من المعدة وثقل البدن لما في الصحيحين عن أبي هريرة إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال «التثاؤب من الشيطان فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع» (۱) والأدب أن يكظمه ما استطاع أي يرده ويحبسه لما روينا، فإن لم يقدر فليضع يده أو كمه على فيه ووضع اليد ثابت في صحيح مسلم ووضع الكم قياس عليه . وصرح في الخلاصة بأنه إن أمكنه عند التثاؤب أن يأخذ شفتيه بسنه فلم يفعل وغطى فاه بيده أو بثوبه يكره . كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة .اهـ. ووجهه أن تغطية الفم منهي عنها في الصلاة لما رواه أبو داود وغيره وإنما أبيحت للضرورة ولا ضرورة إذا أمكنه الدفع، ثم إذا وضع يده على فيه يضع ظهر يده. كذا في مختارات النوازل . قال العلامة الحلبي : وهل يفعل ذلك بيده اليمني أو اليسرى لم أقف عليه مسطوراً لمشايخنا أهـ. وهو عجيب مع كثرة مطالعته للمجتبى ونقله عنه وقد صرح بأنه يغطي فاه بيمينه في القيام وفي غيره بيساره
His saying (the author: and yawning) – with hamza as in al-Sihah. And in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, it is disliked even if outside prayer, mentioned by Miskin because it is from Satan, and the prophets (peace be upon them) are protected from it. His saying: (and yawning) – it is the breath that opens the mouth to expel vapors; it arises from the stomach and heaviness of the body. This is based on the Sahihayn from Abu Huraira that the Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Yawning is from Satan; when one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' The proper conduct is to suppress it as much as possible, i.e., hold it back, as we have narrated. If he cannot, let him place his hand or sleeve over his mouth. Placing the hand is confirmed in Sahih Muslim, and placing the sleeve is analogized to it. In al-Khulasa it is stated that if he is able to bite his lips with his teeth and does not do so, but covers his mouth with his hand or garment, it is disliked. Such is narrated from Abu Hanifa. The reason is that covering the mouth is prohibited in prayer due to what Abu Dawud and others narrated; it is permitted only for necessity, and there is no necessity if he can suppress it. Then, if he places his hand over his mouth, he places its back. So in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. Al-Halabi said: Whether he does this with his right or left hand, I have not found it recorded from our scholars. This is astonishing given his extensive reading of al-Mujtaba and his quoting from it, where it is explicitly stated that he covers his mouth with his right hand when standing and with his left otherwise.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
Passage type: ruling with proof on yawning in prayer. Yawning is disliked in prayer based on the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim: 'Yawning is from Satan; suppress it if possible.' The proper etiquette is to suppress the yawn by closing the mouth or biting the lips. If unable, cover the mouth with the hand or sleeve. The hand should be placed with the back outward. If one could bite his lips but instead covers his mouth, it is disliked (makruh) because covering the mouth unnecessarily is prohibited. The text also notes a difference of opinion on whether to use the right or left hand: some sources specify right hand when standing, left otherwise.

Key Terms
التثاؤب (al-tatha'ub): Yawning, a breath that opens the mouth due to stomach vapors, disliked in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on yawning in prayer?
A) Haram and invalidates prayer
B) Makruh tanzih (disliked)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Sunnah (recommended)

Key Takeaway
Yawning in prayer is disliked (makruh tanzih); the sunna is to suppress it or cover the mouth with the back of the hand.

The Ruling on Imam Standing in the Mihrab: Dislike and Its Reasons
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the reason for dislike of imam in mihrab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two reasons for the dislike (makruh) of the imam standing in the mihrab according to the Hanafi school and identify which reason is relied upon for fatwa.

Core Idea
Imam standing in the mihrab is disliked because it resembles the People of the Book, or because it confuses the congregation.

The Hanafi school, based on Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir, holds that the imam's standing inside the mihrab during prayer is disliked (makruh). However, scholars differed on the reason behind this ruling, leading to two distinct positions. Understanding this dispute helps clarify when the ruling applies and how later authorities settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the imam standing inside the mihrab (the niche) during prayer. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) according to the Hanafi school.
Prostration inside the mihrab is not disliked; only standing.
2
Locate the textual basis
Imam Muhammad explicitly mentioned the dislike in al-Jami' al-Saghir (a Zahir al-Riwayah text) but did not provide a reason. This absence of elaboration led scholars to investigate the cause.
The text in al-Jami' al-Saghir is the primary nass.
3
Understand the two reasons for dislike
Two reasons were proposed: (1) the imam becomes distinguished in place, resembling the practice of the People of the Book; (2) his position becomes ambiguous to those on his right and left. According to the first reason, the ruling is absolute; according to the second, it depends on confusion.
The first reason is based on avoiding resemblance; the second on preventing ambiguity.
4
Evaluate the preferred view
Al-Hidayah and Imam al-Sarakhsi chose the first reason (resemblance) as the most appropriate, making the dislike unconditional. This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
Fath al-Qadir presents a counter-argument that the imam's distinction is actually required by Shari'ah.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
In practice, the imam should avoid standing inside the mihrab while leading prayer, as it is disliked regardless of confusion.
If the mihrab is shallow or does not clearly distinguish the imam, some later scholars argued it may not be disliked, but the cautious position is to avoid it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وقيام الإمام لا سجوده في الطاق) أي المحراب لأن قيامه فيه يشبه صنيع أهل الكتاب بخلاف سجوده فيه وقيامه خارجه. هكذا علل به في الهداية وهو أحد الطريقين للمشايخ، وأصله أن محمداً صرح بالكراهة في الجامع الصغير ولم يفصل، فاختلف المشايخ في سببها فقيل كونه يصير ممتازاً عنهم في المكان لأنه في معنى بيت آخر وذلك صنيع أهل الكتاب. واقتصر عليه في الهداية واختاره الإمام السرخسي وقال : إنه الأوجه . وقيل : اشتباه حاله على من على يمينه ويساره، فعلى الطريقة الأولى يكره مطلقاً، وعلى الثانية لا يكره عند عدم الاشتباه . وفي فتح القدير : ولا يخفي أن امتياز الإمام مقرر مطلوب في الشرع في حق المكان حتى كان التقدم واجباً عليه وغاية ما هنا كونه في خصوص مكان ولا أثر لذلك لأنه يحاذي وسط الصف وهو المطلوب إذ قيامه في غير محاذاته مكروه وغايته اتفاق الملتين في بعض الأحكام، ولا بدع فيه على أن أهل الكتاب إنما
His saying: (and the imam's standing, not his prostration, in the arch) i.e., the mihrab, because his standing in it resembles the practice of the People of the Book, unlike his prostration inside it or his standing outside. This is the reasoning in al-Hidayah, and it is one of two approaches of the scholars. The origin is that Muhammad explicitly stated the dislike in al-Jami' al-Saghir without elaboration. The scholars differed on the reason: some said it is because he becomes distinguished from them in place, as if it is another house, and that is the practice of the People of the Book. Al-Hidayah limited it to this, and Imam al-Sarakhsi chose it, saying it is the most appropriate. Others said: it is because his situation is ambiguous to those on his right and left. According to the first approach, it is disliked absolutely. According to the second, it is not disliked when there is no ambiguity. In Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that the imam's distinction is established and desired in Shari'ah in terms of place; indeed, being ahead is obligatory for him. The extent here is that he is in a specific place, but there is no effect because he aligns with the middle of the row, which is desired. Indeed, his standing not in alignment is disliked. The extent is agreement of the two religions in some rulings, and there is no novelty; indeed, the People of the Book only...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
Passage type: intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of the imam standing inside the mihrab during prayer. Imam Muhammad stated in al-Jami' al-Saghir that it is disliked (makruh) without specifying the reason. Later scholars proposed two reasons: (1) it distinguishes the imam from the congregation, resembling the practice of the People of the Book (Jews and Christians), whose priests stand in a niche; (2) it causes confusion for those beside the imam as to his position. According to the first reason, it is always disliked; according to the second, it is only disliked if confusion results. Al-Hidayah and al-Sarakhsi prefer the first reason. Fath al-Qadir argues that since the imam is supposed to be ahead of the congregation, being in the mihrab is not problematic; it aligns him with the middle of the row, which is desirable. The text ends mid-sentence on page 45.

Key Terms
الطاق (al-tāq): The arch or niche (mihrab) in a mosque where the imam stands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason for the dislike of the imam standing in the mihrab according to al-Hidayah?
A) It confuses the congregation
B) It resembles the practice of the People of the Book
C) It prevents the imam from seeing the congregation
D) It is bid'ah

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the imam's standing in the mihrab is disliked (makruh tanzih) due to resemblance to the People of the Book, and this applies unconditionally.

Ruling on Closing the Eyes in Prayer
Ruling with proof on closing eyes in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on closing the eyes in prayer, identify the evidence cited, and apply the exception for maintaining khushu.

Core Idea
Closing eyes in prayer is makruh tanzih unless needed for concentration.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on closing the eyes during prayer. The author cites a hadith and reasoning from al-Badai to establish that it is disliked (makruh tanzih). However, an important exception is made: if closing the eyes helps preserve khushu (humility) by blocking distracting sights, it is no longer disliked and may even be preferable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taghmīḍ al-‘aynayn (closing both eyes) during prayer. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not prohibited) unless there is a valid reason.
The dislike is not at the level of haram or makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is a hadith narrated by Ibn Adi from Ibn Abbas: 'When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes.' The chain is weak, so the prohibition is softened to dislike.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative (lā yughmiḍ) indicates prohibition, but due to weakness, it indicates dislike. Additionally, the sunnah is to look at the place of prostration; closing abandons this sunnah. Every limb has a role in worship, including the eyes.
The reasoning from al-Badai strengthens the ruling.
4
Note the exception for khushu
If one fears losing khushu due to distracting sights, closing the eyes is not disliked; it may even be better because it aids complete humility.
The exception is based on necessity (darurah) or maslahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتغميض عينيه) لما رواه ابن عدي عن ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا قام أحدكم في الصلاة فلا يغمض عينيه إلا أن في سنده من ضعف . والكراهة مروية عن مجاهد وقتادة. وعلله في البدائع بأن السنة أن . بصره إلى موضع سجوده وفي التغميض ترك هذه السنة، ولأن كل عضو وطرف ذو حظ من هذه العبادة فكذا العين .اهـ. وظاهر كلامهم أن لا يغمض في السجود وقد قال جماعة من الصوفيه نفعنا الله بهم : يفتح عينيه في السجود لأنهما يسجدان . وينبغي أن تكون الكراهة تنزيهية إذا كان لغير ضرورة ولا مصلحة، أما لو خاف فوات خشوع بسبب رؤية ما يفرق الخاطر فلا يكره غمضهما بسبب ذلك بل ربما يكون أولى لأنه حينئذ لكمال الخشوع
His saying: (and closing his eyes) because of what Ibn Adi narrated from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet, 'When one of you stands in prayer, let him not close his eyes,' except that its chain has weakness. And the dislikedness is narrated from Mujahid and Qatada. He explained in al-Badai that the sunnah is that his sight be towards his place of prostration, and in closing the eyes there is abandonment of this sunnah, and because every limb and part has a share in this worship, so too the eye. And the apparent meaning of their statement is that he does not close his eyes in prostration, and a group of Sufis said: he opens his eyes in prostration because they both prostrate. And it is appropriate that the dislike be tanzih if without necessity or benefit; but if he fears losing khushu due to seeing something that distracts the mind, then closing them is not disliked because of that, rather perhaps it is better because then it is for complete humility.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on closing the eyes during prayer. The commentator starts by citing a hadith from Ibn Adi (with a weak chain) that prohibits closing the eyes in prayer. However, the dislike is also transmitted from Mujahid and Qatada. The reasoning from al-Badai is that the sunnah is to look at the place of prostration, and closing the eyes abandons this sunnah. Additionally, every limb has its role in worship, including the eyes. The apparent view is that one should not close even in prostration, but some Sufis argue for opening eyes as the eyes also prostrate. The author concludes that the dislike is tanzih (not to the level of prohibition) when there is no necessity. However, if closing the eyes helps maintain khushu (concentration) by blocking distracting sights, then it is not disliked and may even be better.

Key Terms
تغميض العينين (taghmīḍ al-‘aynayn): The act of closing both eyes during prayer, considered a disliked act unless for concentration.
خشوع (khushu‘): Humility and concentration in prayer, which may justify closing eyes if attained otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is closing the eyes in prayer considered not disliked?
A) During prostration only
B) When it helps maintain khushu by blocking distractions
C) When the imam closes his eyes
D) It is always disliked

Key Takeaway
Closing eyes in prayer is makruh tanzih, but the exception for preserving khushu transforms it into a permissible and sometimes preferred act.
